Frequently asked questions
--------------------------

##### I’m comfortable with Excel. Why should I switch to Grist?

Excel is flexible but fragile. One broken formula or bad copy-paste can mess up your budget. Grist gives you the familiar grid interface you already know but adds a relational structure. This means you update a client or material cost in one place, and it automatically updates across all your job sheets, estimates, and invoices. It’s the flexibility of a spreadsheet without the version chaos.

##### Can my field crew use this on the job site?

Yes. Grist bridges the gap between the field and the office. Because it works in your browser and on tablets, your crew can update daily logs, check material lists, or log hours directly from the site. Updates appear instantly for the project manager in the office, giving you a single, real-time source of truth for the project’s status.

##### Is Grist just for tracking costs, or can it handle project management?

It handles both. You can use Grist as comprehensive construction cost tracking software to monitor budgets versus actuals in real time. But it is also a powerful project management tool. You can build custom views to track RFIs, submittals, and approvals, ensuring your document control is airtight and projects don’t stall waiting for paperwork.

##### Do I need to know how to code to build a custom tool?

No. We believe you should be the architect of your own software without needing a developer. Grist uses a drag-and-drop builder to let you create custom dashboards and workflows. If you do get stuck, our built-in [AI Assistant](https://www.getgrist.com/ai-assistant/)
 can help you write formulas or structure your data, making it easy to build a professional-grade tool yourself.

##### Can I share project schedules with subcontractors without showing them my budget?

Absolutely. This is a key advantage of Grist’s granular access control. You can share a specific view or list with a subcontractor so they can see their tasks and deadlines, while keeping your financial data, markup rates, and other sensitive information completely hidden from them.

##### We have strict data compliance requirements. Where is my data stored?

You have total control. While we offer a secure hosted version, Grist is unique because it offers a [self-hosted option](https://www.getgrist.com/product/self-hosted/)
. If you need complete data independence or have strict IT protocols, you can host Grist on your own private infrastructure, ensuring your proprietary business data never leaves your hands.

# Grist vs Monday: Which is better for work management?

##### Work Management Tool Comparison

Grist vs Monday
===============

Unlike Monday.com, Grist doesn’t stop at tasks. Connect your entire business – data, people, and processes – into one flexible platform built to scale with your needs.

[Get started](https://docs.getgrist.com/welcome/start)

Request demo

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/06/grist-v-monday.png)

What comes after Monday?
------------------------

Monday is built for managing tasks. Grist is built for what comes next for your business.

What begins as a simple tracker often grows into something more – a CRM, a reporting system, or a full operational tool. With Grist, you don’t need to switch tools when your process matures. Add tables, views, logic, rules, custom widgets, and even full applications as your needs grow. No rebuilds. No compromises.

Find your ideal solution
------------------------

#### **Where Monday Shines**

done

Task and project coordination with fast onboarding for teams of any size

done

Built-in views and boards like Kanban, Gantt charts, and calendars

done

Beginner-friendly UI and large template library for easy setup

#### **Where Grist Shines**

done

Relational database structure for clean and secure ingestion

done

Fine-grained access permissions and full ownership of your data

done

Deep customization and integration into unique workflows

Monday vs Grist for work management
-----------------------------------

|     | Monday | Grist |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Core functionality** | Task-centric visual work/project management platform. | Relational spreadsheet-database hybrid. |
| ****Ideal for**** | Teams needing visual task/project tracking. Fast setup and wide team adoption. | Teams needing structured, secure data systems and all-in-one custom workflows. |
| ******Pricing****** | Free plan limited to 2 users; Pro plan starts at $19/user for core features. | Free plan with core features & AI Assistant. Paid plans start at $8/user. |
| ****Data structure**** | Flat task boards with linked items. | Fully relational database that links records across tables natively. |
| ****Flexibility**** | Prebuilt plug-and-play project views, visual customization. | Full control over layout, fields, & relationships. |
| ****Collaboration**** | Team-centric task updates, simple sharing and collaboration. | Real-time editing & per-user access filters. |
| ******Automation****** | No-code “when–then” automation rules. Large catalogue of major software integrations. | REST API. Webhooks. Integration partners (Zapier, n8n, and more). |
| ****Customization**** | Visual only. | Supports formulas, Python scripting, custom widgets. |
| **Hosting & ownership** | Cloud-only. | [Self-hostable](https://www.getgrist.com/product/self-hosted/)<br>. open-source / open-core. SQLite-based. User-controlled data access. |

Organizations needing privacy, security, and flexibility in their solutions

# Custom Manufacturing Software (Open-source) | Grist

##### Grist for Manufacturing

The custom manufacturing software that adapts to your unique product workflow.
==============================================================================

Instead of forcing factory processes into rigid, out-of-the-box software, build the exact tools you need. From inventory tracking to production planning, combine the flexibility of a spreadsheet and the structure of a database. Open-source, self-hostable, and Python-powered.

[Get started](https://docs.getgrist.com/welcome/start)

Request demo

settings

Why settle for manufacturing software that doesn’t fit?
-------------------------------------------------------

done

**Spreadsheets are too fragile:** You love the flexibility, but broken formulas, version conflicts, and data silos are costing you time. A standard spreadsheet can’t handle the complexity of bills of materials (BOMs) or multi-user inventory updates.

done

**ERPs are too rigid:** Traditional manufacturing ERPs are expensive, clunky, and force you to change your workflow to match their software. Customizing them requires expensive consultants and months of development.

done

**The “low-code” sweet spot:** Grist gives you the best of both. You get a relational database that ensures data integrity (like an ERP) with a familiar interface you can customize yourself (like a spreadsheet).

lock

Build your production system, your way
--------------------------------------

done

**Connect your data logic:** Don’t duplicate data. Link your Raw Materials database directly to your Work Orders and Finished Goods. Update a cost in one place, and watch it ripple through every bill of materials instantly.

done

**Design custom views for every team:** Give the shop floor a simple “Check-in/Check-out” card view. Give the purchasing manager a high-level “Low Stock” dashboard. Build custom screens in minutes using drag-and-drop widgets (no IT team required).

done

**Total control, no lock-in:** Need complex logic? Use standard Python formulas to calculate waste percentages, lead times, or pricing tiers. Because Grist is open-source, you own your data and can even self-host for total security and compliance.

Make the most of your data
--------------------------

#### No more silos

The best way to store data is only once and in one place, like a database. But it should also be accessible, like a spreadsheet.

#### Custom solutions

Grow beyond your spreadsheets with flexible, no-code dashboard building. Extend even further with custom views.

#### Ease-of-use

Robust database architecture, with the familiarity of a spreadsheet – formulas included.

#### Secure collaboration

Granular access rules mean that you control permissions down to the cell. Secure collaboration is confident collaboration.

##### Features

Data superpowers
----------------

Streamline your work with Grist’s familar UI and modern feature set.

* * *

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/ai-assistant-formula.gif)

### AI Assistant

The hardest part of working with spreadsheets made easy with AI.

*   Create formulas using plain language.
*   Leverage the power of Python without being an expert.
*   Iterate on formulas using retained conversational context.

[AI spreadsheet assistant](https://www.getgrist.com/ai-assistant/)

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/FlexLayouts5.gif)

### Flexible layout

Arrange your data on screen to maximize your and your team’s productivity.

*   Drag-and-drop widgets to make custom layouts.
*   Link data to quickly pull up details and related records.
*   Turn rows into data cards, and attach relevant images and files.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/AccessRules5.gif)

### Access rules

Collaborate with confidence and peace of mind, using unique system of granular data permissions.

*   Control who sees what, down to each row and column.
*   Share data in part or in full, and still collaborate in real-time.
*   Share limited views of relevant data with third parties.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/Visualization5.gif)

### Visualizations

See what matters at a glance, from big trends to small details.

*   Summarize data into charts or pivot tables to see the big picture.
*   Link charts to update dynamically to visualize segments of data.
*   Show data in new ways with a gallery of custom widgets, or build your own.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/MoreFeatures4.gif)

### More features

Streamline, control, and drill into your data. Discover the endless possibilities of our full-featured relational spreadsheet.  

*   Formulas with Excel functions and Python power.
*   Automatic backups and snapshot history.
*   Conditional styles, and cell formatting.
*   Localized into 12 languages.
*   APIs and integrations.

Frequently asked questions
--------------------------

##### Is Grist suitable for small manufacturing businesses?

Yes. Grist is designed for businesses who have outgrown spreadsheets, including small to mid-sized manufacturers, but aren’t ready for the high cost and rigidity of traditional ERP systems. It offers the flexibility of a spreadsheet with the structure of a database, making it ideal for tracking inventory, production schedules, and orders.

##### How is Grist different from Excel or Google Sheets for manufacturing?

Unlike standard spreadsheets, Grist is a relational database. This means you can store data once and link it everywhere. For example, updating a raw material cost in one table automatically updates every Bill of Materials (BOM) that uses it. You also get granular access controls, allowing you to share specific data with warehouse staff without risking broken formulas or accidental deletions.

##### Can I use Grist for inventory management and BOMs?

Absolutely. Grist’s relational structure is perfect for complex manufacturing workflows like multi-level Bills of Materials (BOMs), inventory depletion, and supply chain tracking. You can use our “[Inventory Tracking](https://www.getgrist.com/templates/inventory-manager/)
” template to get started immediately, or build a completely custom inventory system that matches your exact warehouse layout.

##### Do I need to know Python or coding to use Grist?

No. You can build powerful dashboards and organize data using Grist’s no-code interface and familiar spreadsheet functions. However, if you have unique needs, like complex waste calculations or custom pricing logic, you can use Python formulas to extend Grist’s capabilities far beyond what standard spreadsheets can do.

##### Is Grist open-source?

Yes. Grist’s core is open-source, giving you unprecedented control over your data. You can use our hosted cloud version for convenience, or self-host Grist on your own servers for total data privacy, intranet operation, and compliance.

##### Can Grist integrate with my accounting or shipping software?

Yes. Grist is highly extensible. You can connect to other tools via REST API, webhooks, or integrators like Zapier. This allows you to automatically push completed orders to your shipping platform or sync inventory costs with your accounting software.

##### Is there a free version of Grist?

Yes. Grist offers a full-featured free plan that allows you to build, test, and run your manufacturing workflows without lock-in.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/illustration-gr-clear2.svg)

# Database + spreadsheet = Grist

Database, meet spreadsheet
==========================

Does your infrastructure require a database _and_ spreadsheets? Grist can help.

[Get started](https://public.getgrist.com/signup)

Sync seamlessly
---------------

There’s no avoiding spreadsheets.

But connecting a spreadsheet to a structured database is a hassle, and current spreadsheet-to-database connectors rely on a complex toolchain.

Grist is built on a modern architecture to solve these problems: structured data with the flexibility of a spreadsheet.

![Before and after of current spreadsheet/database workflows compared to Grist.](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/02/comparison3-2048x1308.png)

**Problem:** Spreadsheets aren’t structured or relational
---------------------------------------------------------

database

### **Solution:**  
Grist is a database that feels like a spreadsheet

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/10/icon-leaf@2x.png)

-----------------------------------------------

pin

### **Solution:**  
Grist has all of the common data types

**Problem:** Databases are too technical for most users
-------------------------------------------------------

groups

----------------------------

# Applicant Tracking System Template | Grist

**Applicant Tracking System Template**

[**Open Full Template**](https://templates.getgrist.com/d7NBjwRKqrzp/Recruiting)

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/07/TryMeTR.png)

About the Recruiting Spreadsheet Template
-----------------------------------------

Recruiting is a team project! Coordinate your recruiting efforts with our free, collaborative spreadsheet template. Grist documents like these can be deeply customized and automated [beyond the capabilities of Google Sheets and Excel](https://www.getgrist.com/lookup/)
, so your recruiting team can build the exact workflow you need.

Manage job candidates, resumes, notes, and interviews in one place. Customize the template to suit your organization with guidance from our [Modifying Grist Templates webinar](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=T1Xq4Y2jV50&feature=youtu.be)
.

*   Customize drag and drop layout to match your workflow.
*   Attach resumes directly to the spreadsheet.
*   Capture job descriptions in a notepad integrated into your spreadsheet-database.

How to use this free recruitment tracker spreadsheet template
-------------------------------------------------------------

Use this spreadsheet template to track candidates applying for roles on your team. This can be your centralized hiring hub where you organize candidates, assign tasks to team members, track applicant stages, and pass on candidates.

### How to use the recruiting tracker _Dashboard_ page

Click < and > to select an open position and pull up a list of candidates below.

Add new candidates to the list. You can also add contact information and attach resumes and other documents to the candidate’s card, or [set up a trigger formula to do it for you](https://www.getgrist.com/webinars/trigger-formulas/)
 when a candidate applies.

The cells marked yellow indicate fields that you should fill in with your own recruiting data, and non-yellow cells have been set up to help with calculations or referencing.

![Dashboard page with 4 tables showing an open role being recruited for, as well as candidate information like contact, resume, rating, and stage](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/applicant-tracking-spreadsheet-template-2048x1040.png)

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/recruiting-tracker-template-interactions-table-2048x1225.png)

### How to use the _Interactions_ page

In the ‘Interactions’ card, review and add new interactions by filling in an empty card at the bottom of the widget. Only fill in cells shaded yellow. Candidate’s name, date, and team member’s name will automatically fill in.

On the _Interactions_ page, you can simply see a table of all interactions based on candidate and recruiter. Here you can add notes, applicant stage, rating, or any other criteria your recruiting team uses in the application process.

### How to use the _Roles_ page

In this free recruiting template, you can add new roles in the Roles table, and toggle a role as “Open” to make it available for selection in the dashboard.

To add updates, simply create a new row and enter any relevant job posting information, including new fields necessary for your hiring projects. You can also add relevant information about the role in the notepad below, and include links to the live job postings.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/ATS-template-roles-page-2048x1062.png)

[All spreadsheet templates](https://www.getgrist.com/templates/)

# Access Rules for Teams | Grist

In January, we learned how to create access rules to limit which team members can see or edit which data.

### Timestamps

11:30 Table seed rules  
12:45 Restricting tables with access rules

13:53 What happens to pages and widgets that show restricted tables?  
15:04 Restricting columns with access rules  
16:23 Restricting rows with access rules based on value in cells  
18:52 Restricting data based on users’ login email (the suboptimal way)  
23:22 Creating custom user attributes  
25:26 Restricting data based on users’ login email (the optimal way)  
27:49 Truly locking down structure with access rules  
28:31 Custom user attributes + reference columns  
32:51 Surprise! Troubleshooting. 🤔  
37:06 Anchor links  
39:52 Enable editing a cell, but not erasing a cell, with access rules

# Grist Webinar - Adapting from Spreadsheet to Database

On October 18th, 2021 we held our first Build with Grist webinar, focused on best practices to get the most out of Grist.

Grist CEO Dmitry Sagalovskiy shared tips on adapting data from a spreadsheet to a database using the DRY principle, and building dashboards using linked widgets.

Other topics covered include finding the most recent value from a list of historical records, filtering by several fields, understanding the lookup function and reference lookups, and more.

### Timestamps

00:14 The Ceasar Cipher, encoding secret messages in Grist  
04:05 The DRY principle – best practices in structuring your data  
11:52 Importing spreadsheet data in Grist, and adapting it for a database  
17:37 Creating a reference between related tables  
19:59 Creating dashboards and linking widgets  
27:00 Creating true/false conditional formula columns  
32:07 Grist automatic backups, restoring and saving backups  
35:44 Multi-line Python code  
37:50 Importing Python libraries  
39:10 Entering only times in datetime columns  
43:08 Changing choice columns values based on selection in another column  
46:28 Find the most recent value from a list of historical records e.g more recent product price  
50:34 Filtering by several fields  
52:22 Understanding the lookup function  
56:30 Reference lookups

[](https://www.getgrist.com/webinars/how-dotphoton-built-a-fully-traceable-qa-system-for-the-european-space-agency/)

How Dotphoton built a fully traceable QA system for the European Space Agency
=============================================================================

# Grist Webinar - Trigger Formulas v. Formulas

During November’s webinar, Anais discussed the difference between typical formulas and trigger formulas, and when to use which. She also shared some of her favorite formulas and dove deep into how to use reference columns in lookup formulas.

# Sales Commission Sheet Structure Template (Free and Interactive!)

**Sales Commission Template**

[**Open Full Template**](https://templates.getgrist.com/pVq4xESKtU24/Sales-Commissions-Dashboard/)

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/07/TryMeTR.png)

About the sales commission sheet template
-----------------------------------------

Simplify your sales commission structure and process by allowing sales reps to enter their own data, while this spreadsheet automatically calculates their sales commissions. Dynamic charts reflect revenue and payout data in real-time. Granular permissions ensure sales reps can only access their own sales and commission details, while viewing a leaderboard of total sales by rep.

This Grist spreadsheet template is [more advanced than what a Google Sheet or Excel document is capable of](https://www.getgrist.com/grist-product-comparison/)
, while maintaining a structured format that ensures easy editing and collaboration.

Customize this commission sheet template to match your organization’s needs. Any sales team can tailor this workflow to match their commission structure, no matter how unique. Learn how with our [Modifying Grist Templates webinar](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=T1Xq4Y2jV50&feature=youtu.be)
.

*   Summarize revenue and payout from commission calculations in charts.
*   Look up sales performance by rep with a click to see if sales targets have been met.
*   Access rules limit sales reps to only enter and see their own data and commission structure in detail.

How to use this free commission sheet template
----------------------------------------------

Sales and accounting teams can use this free template to track sales and commission. Sales reps only see their individual sales, and the overall leaderboard. Management can see everything. Be sure to watch our [Sales + Commissions webinar](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jWK4hBXbyKc)
 to learn more.

### How to use the _Sales by Rep_ page

This page is where managers (document owners) and the rest of the sales team (editors or viewers) can see all their recorded sales in a particular time frame, as well as their calculated commission rates and overall payout.

Select a rep and a month to drill into sales. Managers can see all data. However, using preset access rules, reps can only see their sales and commission details, as well as every rep’s total revenue on this leaderboard.

To make updates, team members can easily record their own sales in the ‘Sales’ table at the bottom of this page, including the date, customer, revenue, and any additional relevant information to the sale.

![3 spreadsheet tables on a page showing the highlighted sales performance for a representative](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/Screenshot-2025-07-31-at-2.59.39-PM-2048x1491.png)

![A spreadsheet dashboard showing a bar graph displaying sales performance for the team. Another table shows total sales, and a calculated commission payout.](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/sales-commission-structure-template-2048x1127.png)

### How to use the _Sales Over Time_ page

Only managers can see metrics from the entire sales team over time. This shows all-time sales, and sales broken down by year and month.

This template automatically calculates your performance metrics, including commission rates, monthly sales, and all sales commissions based on the data entered in the ‘Sales’ table within the _Sales by Rep_ page, so you can focus more on insights and reporting.

### How to use the _Customers_ page

This page is a simple CRM to keep customer contact data in one place. Here is where your sales team.

To add updates, simply create a new row and enter any relevant contact information, including new fields necessary for your sales strategy.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/Screenshot-2025-07-31-at-3.03.50-PM-2048x897.png)

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/Screenshot-2025-07-31-at-3.05.04-PM-e1753993275135.png)

### How to use the _Sales by Customer_ page

See the lifetime value of your customers at a glance.

This page references all your listed customers on the _Customers_ page, and then automatically calculates the amount of sales and revenue generated by the sales recorded in the original ‘Sales’ table.

There’s no need to add updates here!

### How to view permissions for this doc’s users

With granular access rules, sales reps only see what’s relevant to them. Click on the “Users” button in the top right to view as any sales rep and compare what they can and cannot view when compared to their manager.

For example, Lance, a preset sales rep, only sees the main leaderboard, personal commission structure, and his own sales performance in the ‘Sales’ table at the bottom. No data will be leaked, and everyone on the sales team can store their data securely and collaboratively in the same place.

To learn more about Grist’s access rules, watch our [comprehensive access rules webinar](https://www.getgrist.com/webinars/access-rules-for-distributed-organizations/)
 covering everything you need to know.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/Screenshot-2025-07-31-at-3.06.20-PM-e1753992443794.png)

Build on your own terms
-----------------------

If you have an existing workflow in tools like Google Sheets or Excel, you can easily import it into this template right away.

Grist’s incremental imports feature allows users to import new activity to existing data, and Grist intelligently combines it without creating duplicates or needing manual cleanup.

[Use This Template](https://templates.getgrist.com/pVq4xESKtU24/Sales-Commissions-Dashboard/)

, and then an interactive custom widget with the [Custom Widget Builder](https://support.getgrist.com/newsletters/2024-10/#custom-widget-builder-widget)

# Grist 2025 - Year in review

Hello and happy holidays from everyone here at Grist Labs!

In addition to shipping new features, we spread our wings to get the word out about what makes Grist special, like with _Spreadsheet Makeover_ and _GristCon_.

We also looked inward – exposing some of our deepest spreadsheet secrets for all to see with our _Grist Secrets_ and _How Grist uses Grist_ webinars.

Read about all of these and more in this year’s recap!

![Year in review hero image](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/2025-year-in-review.png)

Visual learner?
---------------

To view this post in webinar form, check out our [2025 year in review webinar](https://www.getgrist.com/webinars/2025-year-in-review/)
 for an interactive walkthrough of almost all the features mentioned!

Grist by the numbers (of people)
--------------------------------

*   Our [`grist-core`](https://github.com/gristlabs/grist-core)
     GitHub stars went from to 7.4k to over 10.3k. We’re still trying to find a way to convert these stars into goods and services, but in the meantime they decorate our virtual planetarium and dazzle us daily.
*   We went from 300 to over 1,000 Discord community members, and even hosted an entire [virtual conference](https://www.getgrist.com/gristcon-2025/)
     there! [Join them](https://discord.gg/MYKpYQ3fbP)
     (and us!).

Grist for the people
--------------------

**GristCon 2025**

We held our first (but not last!) virtual conference in September, with 10+ talks and sessions by Grist Labs employees and community members.

We even managed to record and upload the results! Check out the recordings [here](https://www.getgrist.com/gristcon-2025/)
.

![GristCon art](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/GristCon-bg.png)

**Spreadsheet Makeover**

Our co-CEO Anais dove into the world of grid-based content creation with a series of [Spreadsheet Makeovers](https://www.youtube.com/@SpreadsheetMakeover)
. By vicariously watching spreadsheets that _aren’t yours_ get assessed and improved, you can sneakily improve your own Grist skills.

[![Spreadsheet makeover](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/sm.gif)](https://www.youtube.com/@SpreadsheetMakeover)

Grist _by_ the people
---------------------

This year we were once again supported by an amazing community that takes advantage of Grist and all its flexibility to assemble and share an ever-growing toolbox. We’ve started capturing community-contributed widgets in [this Grist document](https://grist-marketing.getgrist.com/oHQcp1bG7DS8/Community-Widgets/p/4)
, but we also see lots of cool things shared on [Discord](https://discord.gg/MYKpYQ3fbP)
 and our [Showcase forum](https://community.getgrist.com/c/showcase/8)
.

Featured features
-----------------

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/assistant.gif)

**Assistant upgrades**

Our powerful but unobtrusive [AI Assistant](https://www.getgrist.com/ai-assistant/)
 can now create, modify and analyze your data in addition to helping build Python formulas.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/attachment-storage-transfer.png)

**External attachments**

Push the limits of [Grist attachments](https://support.getgrist.com/document-settings/#external-attachments)
 without pushing Grist.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/admin-controls.gif)

**Admin controls**

A [spreadsheet](https://support.getgrist.com/admin-controls/#admin-controls)
 to manage your spreadsheet management.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/commentsv2-full.gif)

**Comments and Notifications**

[Talk to each other](https://support.getgrist.com/sharing/#comments)
, highlight cells and receive [notifications](https://support.getgrist.com/document-settings/#notifications)
.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/a11y1.gif)

**Accessibility improvements**

The credit for this important work goes to [Emanuel Pelletier](https://github.com/manuhabitela)
, who’s made so many improvements that we had to add a new infopane (hit F4).

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/suggestions.gif)

**Suggestions**

A whole new way to [collaborate on relational data](https://support.getgrist.com/sharing/#suggestions)
. A version of version control. Structured and sanitized data crowdsourcing. More to come in 2026…

How about a quick list of other 2025 features/improvements that didn’t make the cut: improved link previews, duplicating widgets, row height controls, document tours tutorials, attachment pasting, user presence, [F O C U S M O D E](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qrohjlHIE74)
, saving page collapse state, hidden and prefilled fields for Forms, lots of date shortcuts, a service accounts API, self-hosted user and document disabling.

Webinar highlights
------------------

One of the best parts about doing a monthly webinar is how we’re compelled to both dig deep into Grist’s inner workings, but also reactively respond to what users are asking about or working on at any given moment. This led to some unusually introspective exposes where everyone who works on Grist shared their trips, tricks, workflows and nightmares. It also gave us a long-due opportunity to spotlight user-created custom widgets.

[](https://www.getgrist.com/webinars/grist-secrets/)

Grist Secrets 🤫
================

Webinar 07.29.25

2026
----

There are two things to look out for as we head into the next year: the **next iteration of GristCon** and our experimental **Suggestions** feature. We say this not only to build excitement, but because we want your input on both! Do you have a pitch for the next GristCon? Have you played around with Suggestions? A complaint about either? Please get in touch via our [Contact page](https://www.getgrist.com/contact/)
 or on Discord!

As always, you can check our [GitHub roadmap](https://github.com/gristlabs/grist-core/projects/1)
 to see _some_ of what we’re working on, though rest assured the “labs” part of Grist Labs is and has always been important.

Happy new year!  

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/Grist-Favicon.png)

[](https://www.getgrist.com/blog/spreadsheet-suggestions/)

# Grist 2023 - Year In Review | Grist

Hello and happy holidays from everyone here at Grist Labs!

It was a big year for Grist. We gained more users than ever and shipped a bunch of features.

We also had the privilege of finding out how Grist is being used all over the world, from within the civil service to hobby groups to IT infrastructure management.

Highlights
----------

*   🌌 Our GitHub stars went from 3.4 to 5.6k – a 60% increase!
*   🗣️ We were featured on [Hacker News’ frontpage](https://news.ycombinator.com/item?id=38080951)
     for the second time and got invaluable, unvarnished feedback as always.
*   🇫🇷 We had the privilege to present Grist alongside [ANCT](https://agence-cohesion-territoires.gouv.fr/)
     at NEC 2023 in Bordeaux, to talk about open-source and no-code tools, and the [digital commons](https://www.getgrist.com/digital-commons/)
    .
*   💬 We launched our [official Discord server](https://discord.gg/MYKpYQ3fbP)
     to chat with our growing community.

Product milestones
------------------

Most importantly, Grist itself took a huge leap this year. Both internal work and community contributions have improved Grist drastically, not only polishing existing features but setting the groundwork for exciting developments (see some hints at the bottom of this post). Here are some highlights, limited to one per month:

translate

**January** – we started our [Weblate project](https://hosted.weblate.org/engage/grist/)
, and thanks to dozens of contributors are up to 21 active translations.

atr

**February** – we released the first version of Grist’s [standalone Electron app](https://github.com/gristlabs/grist-electron)
.

team\_dashboard

**March** – the launch of one of our most popular templates – [Flashcards](https://www.getgrist.com/templates/flashcards-template/)
.

open\_in\_browser

**April** – we published our [`grist-static` repo](https://github.com/gristlabs/grist-static)
, letting you host `.grist` files without the full back-end.

webhook

**May** – Grist grows claws with better UI support for [webhooks](https://support.getgrist.com/newsletters/2023-05/#webhooks)
.

ads\_click

**June** – in what became known as “the summer of selectors”, we added [highlights for selector rows](https://support.getgrist.com/newsletters/2023-06/#highlighting-for-selector-rows)
 and made other improvements to widget linking.

smart\_toy

**July** – though not as exciting or trendy as selectors, we launched our [AI Formula Assistant](https://www.getgrist.com/ai-assistant/)
.

table\_view

**August** – building on `grist-static` – and in an effort to free the CSV – we released the [Grist CSV Viewer](https://www.getgrist.com/csv-viewer/)
.

calendar\_month

**September** – the time finally came for us to release the official [Grist calendar widget](https://support.getgrist.com/widget-calendar/)
.

search

**October** – [way too much happened this month](https://support.getgrist.com/newsletters/2023-10/)
, but let’s highlight [formula lookups & shortcuts](https://support.getgrist.com/newsletters/2023-10/#formula-shortcuts)
.

open\_in\_new

**November** – relational navigation within Grist got much easier with [Record Cards](https://support.getgrist.com/record-cards/)
.

how\_to\_vote

**December** – (rumbling noise heard in the distance) forms … forms … FORMS! … **\*FORMS!\***

Community contributions
-----------------------

One of the best parts of [Grist’s open-source principles](https://www.getgrist.com/about/)
 is working with others across the globe who understand what we’re trying to do. We’d like to shout out some of the many community contributions over the year that greatly enhance the product and bring us tremendous inspiration:

*   [@jperon](https://github.com/jperon)
    ‘s [QR code widget](https://support.getgrist.com/newsletters/2023-08/#community-highlights)
    , [custom SQL selector widget](https://community.getgrist.com/t/custom-widget-with-pug-python-and-parcel-js/3275)
    , [advanced search widget](https://community.getgrist.com/t/filter-by-formula/3212)
     using `eval`, and – last but not least – his tireless Advent of Code Grist mastery shared on [our Discord](https://discord.gg/MYKpYQ3fbP)
     (in the `#advent-of-code` channel).
*   [@enthus1ast](https://github.com/enthus1ast)
    ‘s [app that periodically backs up Grist documents](https://github.com/enthus1ast)
     in SQLite, XLSX, and CSV file formats, Grist [infrastructure monitoring system daemon](https://community.getgrist.com/t/infrastructure-monitoring-with-grist/2866)
    , and Nim [REST API client](https://community.getgrist.com/t/grist-api-client-for-nim-lang/2927)
    .
*   Two custom calendar widgets from [@ToJans](https://twitter.com/ToJans/status/1638156999249502215)
     and [@wunter8](https://community.getgrist.com/t/simple-calendar-widget/2676)
     that helped direct us towards making [our own](https://support.getgrist.com/widget-calendar/)
    . You two made it look easy! Calendars are surprisingly complicated!
*   [@johncant](https://github.com/johncant)
    ’s [PostgreSQL Foreign Data Wrapper](https://community.getgrist.com/t/postgresql-grist-fdw/2678)
    , which is a very neat tool that allows you to import and query Grist tables in PostgreSQL.
*   Leonard\_Gallion’s handy Python code that lets you [download documents as .grist files](https://community.getgrist.com/t/basic-python-code-to-download-documents-as-grist-files/2929)
    .
*   [@CoverWhale](https://github.com/CoverWhale)
     Grist Go client, [Gorist](https://github.com/CoverWhale/gorist)
    . (we’ll never get over the name)
*   [@inducer](https://github.com/inducer)
    ‘s trio of Grist utils:
    *   [grist-availability](https://github.com/inducer/grist-availability/)
        : a tool to help with multi-person scheduling using the new calendar widget.
    *   [grist-mailmerge](https://github.com/inducer/grist-mailmerge/)
        : a batch emailer driven by a Grist table and a Jinja template.
    *   [pygrist-mini](https://github.com/inducer/pygrist-mini)
        : a tiny Grist API client for Python.

Finally, a huge thanks to our collaborators at ANCT for their many PRs, and to all of our Weblate translation contributors.

2024 – What’s coming next
-------------------------

Our [GitHub roadmap](https://github.com/gristlabs/grist-core/projects/1)
 is the best way to keep track of what we’re actually working on, but here are a few topics that we’re constantly thinking about:

![What's on Grist's brain: Easier self-hosting; WYSIWYS; Custom domains; Theming; Timezones.](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/12/brain.png)

Wait…what’s WYSIWYS? [Ask us on Discord.](https://discord.gg/MYKpYQ3fbP)
  
  
See you next year! 🫡

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/Grist-Favicon.png)

[](https://www.getgrist.com/blog/spreadsheet-suggestions/)

Why don’t suggestions or tracked changes work in spreadsheets?
==============================================================

01.26.26

# How to migrate your data from Airtable without losing linked records

Airtable data migration
=======================

##### Preserving healthy relationships

Export your Airtable data, links and attachments into a platform you control.

[Migrate now for free](https://docs.getgrist.com/welcome/start)

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/hero.png)

1\. Add new
-----------

Select “Import from Airtable”.

2\. Authorize
-------------

Authorize using “Connect with Airtable” or a private access token.

3\. Select data
---------------

Select which base and tables to import. Keep all data, just the structure, or skip a table entirely.

4\. Import
----------

Data, attachments, and relationships, all in a spreadsheet that you control.

That’s it!
----------

Once your data’s in Grist, it can actually be yours. Self-host for complete sovereignty, and take advantage of all of [Grist’s other advantages](https://www.getgrist.com/lookup/grist-vs-airtable/)
 to see why people are migrating.

[Sign up for free](https://docs.getgrist.com/welcome/start)

Learn more
----------

45-minute webinar with many more examples (including real-life workflows).

High level Grist overview.

Why Grist? It minds its business.
---------------------------------

check

Self-hosting option for complete data control

check

Access rules enforced at API and database level, not just UI

check

Open-source codebase allows security auditing

check

Comprehensive [admin controls](https://support.getgrist.com/admin-controls/)
 for workspace, user and document management (Enterprise plans only)

[Consult an expert](https://www.getgrist.com/contact/)

[Get started for free](https://docs.getgrist.com/welcome/start)

[![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/Grist-Logo-White.png)](https://www.getgrist.com/)

*   [Twitter](https://twitter.com/getgrist)
    
*   [LinkedIn](https://www.linkedin.com/company/grist-labs/)
    
*   [Facebook](https://www.facebook.com/getgrist)

# AI for Spreadsheets (Tools That Go Beyond Excel)

##### beyond excel & Basic spreadsheets

AI for spreadsheets
===================

Can your spreadsheet’s AI tool handle relational data? While Excel has Copilot, and Google Sheets, Gemini, Grist has embedded AI that understands data structure; not just cells.

[Get started](https://docs.getgrist.com/welcome/start)

[Request demo](https://www.getgrist.com/contact/)

![screenshot of Grist's AI Assistant for spreadsheets interface](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/assistant-popup.png)

### [AI spreadsheet assistant](https://www.getgrist.com/ai-assistant/)

Say hello to Grist’s AI Assistant, your context-aware collaborator, available under the ‘Tools’ menu in the left-hand navigation panel of every document.

Simply describe what you’re trying to do, and the assistant will guide you through it.

[Say hello](https://www.getgrist.com/ai-assistant/)

![screenshot of the ai spreadsheet generator chat interface](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/ai-spreadsheet-template-generator-2.png)

### [AI spreadsheet generator](https://www.getgrist.com/ai/spreadsheet-generator/)

Watch Grist’s AI bring your spreadsheet ideas to life – no coding knowledge required.

Bring a vision of a template and enter a prompt, and Grist’s AI handles the rest.

[Start exploring](https://www.getgrist.com/ai/spreadsheet-generator/)

### [AI spreadsheet data visualization](https://www.getgrist.com/ai/spreadsheet-data-visualization/)

Grist’s AI builds the Python-powered summaries you need to visualize insights from your spreadsheets, all using natural language.

Learn how automated data preparation meets user-driven visualization on Grist.

[Start visualizing](https://www.getgrist.com/ai/spreadsheet-data-visualization/)

![screenshot of using the AI Assistant for spreadsheet data visualization](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/ai-spreadsheet-data-visualization-grist.png)

![screenshot of using the AI assistant for spreadsheet data cleaning](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/ai-data-cleaning-spreadsheets-grist-3.png)

### [AI data cleaning for spreadsheets](https://www.getgrist.com/ai/data-cleaning/)

Grist natively supports data cleaning through intelligent imports, relational structures, and formula transformations for consistency.

Learn how the AI enhances this power through natural language commands.

[Start data cleaning](https://www.getgrist.com/ai/data-cleaning/)

Grist is built for modern data workflows
----------------------------------------

Spreadsheet AI that understands structure, not just cells.

done

**Spreadsheet familiarity, database power  
**When inventory affects orders affects forecasting (for example), Grist maintains these connections automatically — and the AI tool understands the relationships.

done

**Build custom apps without coding**  
Create the exact workflow your team needs. The AI tool helps construct pages, prepare data for charts, and link data views through simple conversation.

done

**Python power, natural language interface**  
Access Python’s capabilities by describing what you need. Grist’s AI generates formulas using the standard library — from basic calculations to data transformations.

![grist product explanation Venn diagram](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/Grist-vs.-Everyone-Venn2-2-800x696-1.png)

One spreadsheet, converging AI-powered solutions
------------------------------------------------

From creating summary tables with specified GROUP BY columns to generating Python and Excel formulas to linking widgets on the same page, Grist’s AI adapts to how your relational data actually works.

[Pricing](https://www.getgrist.com/pricing/)

Transform data chaos into structured intelligence
-------------------------------------------------

#### Core capabilities, now AI-powered:

done

**Data standardization made simple**  
Inconsistent date formatting? Poor naming conventions? The AI identifies patterns and suggests fixes across related tables — maintaining referential integrity where Excel cannot.

done

**From flat files to relational structure**  
Import data chaos. The AI helps identify relationships, suggest table structures, and build relations — transforming isolated data into a connected system.

done

**Collaborative without conflicts**  
Multiple users, different permissions, one source of truth. The AI helps set up views and access patterns, preventing the version nightmares plaguing shared spreadsheets.

done

**Scale without breaking  
**As data grows from hundreds to hundreds of thousands of rows, Grist maintains performance. The AI helps create efficient summaries and manage complexity at scale.

![graphic representing AI for spreadsheets with Grist](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/ai-for-spreadsheets.png)

More on Grist + AI
------------------

[](https://www.getgrist.com/webinars/build-your-document-with-ai/)

Build Your Document with AI
===========================

Webinar 10.28.25

Frequently asked questions
--------------------------

##### How does Grist’s AI compare to Excel Copilot?

**Excel Copilot** is limited to generating text summaries and basic content within cells. Microsoft [explicitly warns against](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/office/copilot-function-5849821b-755d-4030-a38b-9e20be0cbf62#ID0EDBBJ)
 using it for “any task requiring accuracy or reproducibility,” especially numerical calculations.  
  
**Grist’s AI** understands relational data structures, creates Python formulas for complex calculations, builds document architecture (pages, widgets, summaries), and modifies data with undo support. Unlike Copilot’s text-only focus, Grist’s AI works with your actual data relationships.

##### What are the usage limits and pricing?

**Grist AI:**

*   Additional credits: 500 for $10/month or 2,000 for $29/month
*   Free plan: 100 AI credits (lifetime)
*   Pro plan ($8-10/user/month): 100 credits/month
*   Business plan ($24-30/user/month): 2,000 credits/month

**Excel Copilot Pro:**

*   $20/user/month (requires Microsoft 365 subscription)
*   Limited to 100 calls per 10 minutes or 300 calls per hour

##### Can I import my existing Excel files?

Yes. Grist imports Excel (.xlsx) and CSV files directly. The AI can help restructure flat spreadsheet data into proper relational tables, maintaining all your existing information while adding database capabilities Excel lacks.

##### Do I need to know Python to use Grist’s AI

No. The AI writes Python formulas from your plain English descriptions. You describe what you need i.e, “calculate the moving average of sales for the last 3 months” and the AI generates the Python code using the full standard library.

##### Is my Spreadsheet data sent to AI servers?

Your data is sent to OpenAI only when you actively submit a request to the AI Assistant. You control exactly when and what data is shared.

##### What can’t Grist’s AI do?

The AI Assistant cannot:

*   Make structural changes to access rules (though Grist has granular permissions)
*   Automatically monitor changes without prompting
*   Access external APIs or live web data directly
*   Generate advanced machine learning models (though it can write Python for data analysis)

##### Why can’t Excel Copilot handle numerical calculations?

Microsoft [acknowledges](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/office/copilot-function-5849821b-755d-4030-a38b-9e20be0cbf62#ID0EDBBJ)
 Copilot’s tendency to hallucinate and generate incorrect responses, making it unsuitable for financial reporting, legal documents, or any high-stakes calculations. Grist’s AI, working with structured data and Python’s deterministic functions, provides reliable, reproducible calculations.

##### Can multiple users work with AI simultaneously?

Yes. Grist’s real-time collaboration means multiple team members can use the AI Assistant in the same document, with each person’s changes tracked and reversible. Excel Copilot works only for individual licensed users.

##### Is Grist available offline or self-hosted?

Unlike Excel’s cloud-dependent Copilot, Grist offers self-hosting options. The full edition of Grist can be run on your own servers with the AI Assistant, maintaining complete data sovereignty. Excel Copilot requires cloud connectivity and cannot be self-hosted.

# AI Formula Generation - Solving Spreadsheets' Biggest Headache

**Update Jul. 24 2023:** Grist has launched an integrated [AI spreadsheet assistant](https://www.getgrist.com/ai-assistant/)
, so you can try this experiment for yourself!

Curious to explore AI formula generation, Grist’s R&D team recently experimented with [OpenAI](https://openai.com/)
 and a prompt generation strategy to see how well AI could write formulas in Grist. While this AI-assisted formula generation feature isn’t yet a part of Grist, this experiment proves its future value. The experiment demonstrates how AI can eliminate a common struggle for today’s spreadsheet user — writing formulas correctly. 

_**Imagine if writing spreadsheet formulas were as simple as asking a question**_.

If you ask a spreadsheet fan what they like about them, there’s a good chance they’ll mention formulas. Spreadsheets are the original low-code platform – sprinkle in a little bit of code and you get a big benefit. But that little bit of code can be daunting and unapproachable.

An overview of the Grist Labs AI Formula Generation Experiment

We see plenty of Grist power users who use every Grist feature except [formulas](https://support.getgrist.com/formulas/)
, which seems a shame. People may find it easy to write a formula to add two numbers, but how do they uncover in which quarter a date resides? Or how to fix those missing leading zeros in a column of zip codes? Not to be dramatic, but users are in for a time-sucking mind-numbing rabbit hole of searching the internet for tips. AI might be the solution to this common spreadsheet headache!

AI formula prompts are written in plain English, or other languages.

Spreadsheet formulas expressed in Python
----------------------------------------

In recent years, AI large language models have gotten quite good at interpreting language and writing code, with many programmers using them routinely. We wondered – could advances in AI be applied to writing spreadsheet formulas in Grist? We wanted to uncover whether AI could bridge the gap between what the user needs a formula to do, as expressed in plain English, and the formula that delivers the correct result. 

While spreadsheet formula writing bots [aren’t new](https://excelformulabot.com/)
, Grist is an evolution of spreadsheets with a unique opportunity because we support Python for writing our formulas. Grist formulas lift up Excel functions to a new level with the full power of Python. Current AI models are particularly good at Python because there are vast quantities of Python code on the internet to train these models on. 

As the most popular programming language today and the best for beginners, Python was an essential choice for Grist, unlocking many possibilities for a large audience. Python is much more capable than spreadsheet functions at data analysis and data manipulation – greatly expanding what’s possible in Grist. 

The AI-generated formula could teach a novice new Python syntax to use in their own formulas.

Relational data
---------------

Another significant advantage of Grist over traditional spreadsheets is its clear structure, with named tables, columns, and relationships between them. Each document is essentially a relational database, with its schema neatly described in Python in Grist’s unique “Code View” feature. All this is available to the bot, helping it understand the data and make inferences.

With spreadsheet formula bots like ExcelFormulaBot, prompts must often specify which columns or ranges should be included in the formula because spreadsheet schema is undefined. In Grist, the prompt doesn’t need to mention specific columns. This is because the AI can look at the tables’ schema, interpret the data, and guess which columns to use in the formula.

AI large language models can make inferences based on prompt and Grist document structure.

The AI Formula Generation Experiment
------------------------------------

The team tested the experiment using documents and formulas found in our [template gallery](https://templates.getgrist.com/)
_._ The AI-generated formulas were correct 36 out of 48 times in the minimal experiment test dataset. That experimentation suggested ways to improve this, such as writing column meta descriptions – an exciting path to look forward to. You can view the [results of the AI experiment](https://public.getgrist.com/n3jAtRYDSVWe/AI-Formula-dataset)
.

Even when the formula was incorrect, it was often close enough that a Python novice could read the formula to understand how to tweak it to produce the correct result. The AI-generated formula can also demonstrate new ways to write code, which teaches key concepts to beginners.

Need to write a formula? Just ask!
----------------------------------

AI has left the realm of science fiction. The future may offer spreadsheet formula writing that is as simple as asking a question, thanks to AI. Today, many professionals, such as programmers and artists, use AI as a part of everyday tasks, reducing the friction of getting the job done. With AI-generated spreadsheet formulas, Grist users may soon join those who use AI casually daily – we think that’s pretty cool.

If you’re a Grist self-hoster with an [API key to OpenAI](https://beta.openai.com/overview)
, that day has arrived – play with the experiment yourself! You can find the [AI experiment on GitHub](https://github.com/gristlabs/grist-core/pull/345)
.

[](https://www.getgrist.com/blog/spreadsheet-suggestions/)

# Workflow automations | Grist

Workflow automation in Grist
============================

Data-driven workflows – no code or manual intervention required.

[Try automations for free](https://docs.getgrist.com/billing/create-team/price_1PIxMTErFFRdaVEUSc0NXB0O)

What Grist automations let you do
---------------------------------

flag

Automatically trigger actions like emails and webhooks when your data changes

cable

Build action-based workflows with external services such as n8n, Zapier and Make

history

Monitor live triggers and view automation history

Automation in three steps
-------------------------

##### Trigger + condition = action

1
=

Create a data **trigger** when rows are added, removed or updated.

2
=

Specify **conditions** and **filters** to make sure your automations only fire when needed.

3
=

Design **actions** that send dynamic emails to collaborators, or connect to external services with webhooks.

Integrations
------------

##### Unlock your data with external services

Grist’s automations can plug into countless external services using webhooks. These are triggerable the same way as dynamic email – you set conditions for specific changes in your document, whether adding, removing or modifying data.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/n8n.png)

### n8n

Good for technical teams who are comfortable with low-code workflows, and organizations that need to be able to self-host.

See our [video walkthroughs](https://www.getgrist.com/automations/#videos)
 for examples.

### Zapier

Enterprise-level automations with tight AI integration, and likely the _most_ integrations.

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/zapier.png)

![](https://www.getgrist.com/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/make.png)

### Make

A less expensive option, but well-suited for complex workflows.

Enterprise-grade security built-in
----------------------------------

check

Self-hosting option for complete data control

check

Granular [role-based access rules](https://www.getgrist.com/role-based-access-controls/)
 for confident collaboration

check

Open-source core and full source available for security auditing

check

Export restrictions respect access rules (unlike column hiding)

check

Comprehensive [admin controls](https://support.getgrist.com/admin-controls/)
 for workspace, user and document management
